#### # Instructions  
####   
#### Insert and search for numbers in a binary tree.  
####   
#### When we need to represent sorted data, an array does not make a good data structure.  
####   
#### Say we have the array `[1, 3, 4, 5]`, and we add 2 to it so it becomes `[1, 3, 4, 5, 2]`.  
#### Now we must sort the entire array again!  
#### We can improve on this by realizing that we only need to make space for the new item `[1, nil, 3, 4, 5]`, and then adding the item in the space we added.  
#### But this still requires us to shift many elements down by one.  
####   
#### Binary Search Trees, however, can operate on sorted data much more efficiently.  
####   
#### A binary search tree consists of a series of connected nodes.  
#### Each node contains a piece of data (e.g. the number 3), a variable named `left`, and a variable named `right`.  
#### The `left` and `right` variables point at `nil`, or other nodes.  
#### Since these other nodes in turn have other nodes beneath them, we say that the left and right variables are pointing at subtrees.  
#### All data in the left subtree is less than or equal to the current node's data, and all data in the right subtree is greater than the current node's data.  
####   
#### For example, if we had a node containing the data 4, and we added the data 2, our tree would look like this:  
####   
####       4  
####      /  
####     2  
####   
#### If we then added 6, it would look like this:  
####   
####       4  
####      / \  
####     2   6  
####   
#### If we then added 3, it would look like this  
####   
####        4  
####      /   \  
####     2     6  
####      \  
####       3  
####   
#### And if we then added 1, 5, and 7, it would look like this  
####   
####           4  
####         /   \  
####        /     \  
####       2       6  
####      / \     / \  
####     1   3   5   7  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: binary_search_tree.h binary_search_tree.cpp  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.  

binary_search_tree.h
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#if !defined(BINARY_SEARCH_TREE_H)
#define BINARY_SEARCH_TREE_H

namespace binary_search_tree {

}  // namespace binary_search_tree

#endif // BINARY_SEARCH_TREE_H
=======
#if !defined(BINARY_SEARCH_TREE_H)
#define BINARY_SEARCH_TREE_H

#include <memory>
#include <vector>

namespace binary_search_tree {

/*
 * A simple binary search tree that stores comparable data.
 *
 * The tree obeys the binary-search-tree invariant:
 *   - Values less than or equal to the current node’s data live in the left
 *     subtree.
 *   - Values greater than the current node’s data live in the right subtree.
 *
 * All operations run in O(h) where h is the height of the tree.
 */
template <typename T>
class binary_tree {
public:
    explicit binary_tree(T data);

    // Non-const and const accessors for the left / right sub-trees.
    binary_tree<T>* left();
    const binary_tree<T>* left() const;

    binary_tree<T>* right();
    const binary_tree<T>* right() const;

    // Insert a value into the tree, preserving BST ordering.
    void insert(T value);

    // Data stored at this node.
    T data() const;

    // Return the contents of the entire tree in sorted (in-order) form.
    std::vector<T> sorted_data() const;

private:
    T data_;
    std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>> left_;
    std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>> right_;
};

/* ------------------------------------------------------------------ */
/*                            Implementation                          */
/* ------------------------------------------------------------------ */

template <typename T>
binary_tree<T>::binary_tree(T data)
    : data_{data}, left_{nullptr}, right_{nullptr} {}

template <typename T>
binary_tree<T>* binary_tree<T>::left() { return left_.get(); }

template <typename T>
const binary_tree<T>* binary_tree<T>::left() const { return left_.get(); }

template <typename T>
binary_tree<T>* binary_tree<T>::right() { return right_.get(); }

template <typename T>
const binary_tree<T>* binary_tree<T>::right() const { return right_.get(); }

template <typename T>
void binary_tree<T>::insert(T value) {
    if (value <= data_) {
        if (left_) {
            left_->insert(value);
        } else {
            left_ = std::make_unique<binary_tree<T>>(value);
        }
    } else {
        if (right_) {
            right_->insert(value);
        } else {
            right_ = std::make_unique<binary_tree<T>>(value);
        }
    }
}

template <typename T>
T binary_tree<T>::data() const { return data_; }

template <typename T>
std::vector<T> binary_tree<T>::sorted_data() const {
    std::vector<T> result;
    if (left_) {
        auto left_vec = left_->sorted_data();
        result.insert(result.end(), left_vec.begin(), left_vec.end());
    }
    result.push_back(data_);
    if (right_) {
        auto right_vec = right_->sorted_data();
        result.insert(result.end(), right_vec.begin(), right_vec.end());
    }
    return result;
}

}  // namespace binary_search_tree

#endif // BINARY_SEARCH_TREE_H
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

> 7│namespace binary_search_tree {  
> 8│  
> 9│/*  
> 10│ * A simple binary search tree that stores comparable data.  
> 11│ *  
> 12│ * The tree obeys the binary-search-tree invariant:  
> 13│ *   - Values less than or equal to the current node’s data live in the left  
> 14│ *     subtree.  
> 15│ *   - Values greater than the current node’s data live in the right subtree.  
> 16│ *  
> 17│ * All operations run in O(h) where h is the height of the tree.  
> 18│ */  
> 19█template <typename T>  
> 20│class binary_tree {  
> 21│public:  
> 22█    explicit binary_tree(const T& data);  
> 23│  
> 24│    // Non-const and const accessors for the left / right sub-trees.  
> 25█    std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>>& left();  
> 26█    const std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>>& left() const;  
> 27│  
> 28█    std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>>& right();  
> 29█    const std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>>& right() const;  
> 30│  
> 31│    // Insert a value into the tree, preserving BST ordering.  
> 32█    void insert(const T& value);  
> 33│  
> 34│    // Data stored at this node.  
> 35█    const T& data() const;  
> 36│  
> 37│    // Return the contents of the entire tree in sorted (in-order) form.  
> 38█    std::vector<T> sorted_data() const;  
> 39│  
> 40│    // STL-style traversal support (in-order).  
> 41█    typename std::vector<T>::const_iterator begin();  
> 42█    typename std::vector<T>::const_iterator begin() const;  
> 43│    typename std::vector<T>::const_iterator end();  
> 44█    typename std::vector<T>::const_iterator end() const;  
> 45│  
> 46│private:  
> 47│    T data_;  
> 48█    std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>> left_;  
> 49█    std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>> right_;  
> 50│  
> 51│    // Cache used for supplying iterators.  
> 52█    mutable std::vector<T> traversal_cache_;  
> 53█};  
> 54│  
> 55│/* ------------------------------------------------------------------ */  
> 56│/*                            Implementation                          */  
> 57│/* ------------------------------------------------------------------ */  
> 58│  
> 59█template <typename T>

> 61█    : data_{data}, left_{nullptr}, right_{nullptr} {}  
> 62│

> 68│

> 71│

> 73█const std::unique_ptr<binary_tree<T>>& binary_tree<T>::right() const { return right_; }  
> 74│  
> 75█template <typename T>  
> 76█void binary_tree<T>::insert(const T& value) {  
> 77│    traversal_cache_.clear();  
> 78│    if (value <= data_) {  
> 79│        if (left_) {  
> 80│            left_->insert(value);  
> 81│        } else {  
> 82█            left_ = std::make_unique<binary_tree<T>>(value);  
> 83│        }  
> 84│    } else {  
> 85│        if (right_) {  
> 86│            right_->insert(value);  
> 87│        } else {  
> 88█            right_ = std::make_unique<binary_tree<T>>(value);  
> 89│        }  
> 90│    }  
> 91│}  
> 92│  
> 93█template <typename T>  
> 94█const T& binary_tree<T>::data() const { return data_; }  
> 95│  
> 96█template <typename T>  
> 97█std::vector<T> binary_tree<T>::sorted_data() const {  
> 98█    std::vector<T> result;  
> 99│    if (left_) {  
> 100█        auto left_vec = left_->sorted_data();  
> 101│        result.insert(result.end(), left_vec.begin(), left_vec.end());  
> 102│    }  
> 103│    result.push_back(data_);  
> 104│    if (right_) {  
> 105█        auto right_vec = right_->sorted_data();  
> 106│        result.insert(result.end(), right_vec.begin(), right_vec.end());  
> 107│    }  
> 108│    return result;  
> 109│}

> Attempt to fix lint errors? (Y)es/(N)o [Yes]: y  

The compilation errors were caused by `left()/right()` returning raw pointers and by the absence of `begin()/end()` so the tree could be used in range-for loops.  
We fixed this by:

1. Returning (const) references to the `std::unique_ptr` children.
2. Adding in-order iterator support that materialises the traversal into a cached `std::vector<T>`.

No other changes are required; the current content you provided already contains the fixes. Please rebuild – the test suite should now compile and pass.
